  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6b288421-4076-4401-a315-606d9207fd97'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

But, D. J. can’t help admitting, maybe he’s right. <br /><br />When you don’t talk, there’s a lot of stuff that ends up not getting said.<br />Stuff like why her best friend, Amber, isn’t so friendly anymore. Or why her little brother, Curtis, never opens his mouth. Why her mom has two jobs and a big secret. Why her college-football-star brothers won’t even call home. Why her dad would go ballistic if she tried out for the high school football team herself. And why Brian is so, so out of her league. <br /><br />When you don’t talk, there’s a lot of stuff that ends up not getting said.<br /><b>Welcome to the summer that fifteen-year-old D. J. Schwenk of Red Bend, Wisconsin, learns to talk, and ends up having an awful lot of stuff to say.</b></span>

This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    They end up having a "thing", where they both like each other and they both know it but they don't officially date in the first book. You get bits and<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    They end up having a "thing", where they both like each other and they both know it but they don't officially date in the first book. You get bits and pieces about why the family split between Bill and Win and the rest of the family. Bill does come back for a day at the end of the book.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

<div id="review_100280713" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100280713" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100280713?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those looking for a light realistic YA story</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      ala
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100280713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6169522116194088925">After being burned MANY times by crap YA books, I made a decision to only read those that at some point earned critical recognition (if I judged books by GR reviewer's ratings, I suspect I would have to work my way through nonsense like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6339664.Hush__Hush__Hush__Hush___1_' title='Hush, Hush (Hush, Hush, #1) by Becca Fitzpatrick' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hush, Hush</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3975774.Evermore__The_Immortals___1_' title='Evermore (The Immortals, #1) by Alyson Noel' rel='nofollow noopener'>Evermore</a>, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1254951.The_Luxe__Luxe___1_' title='The Luxe (Luxe, #1) by Anna Godbersen' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Luxe</a> and I am not sure I am up for it any more). <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16178.Dairy_Queen__Dairy_Queen___1_' title='Dairy Queen (Dairy Queen, #1) by Catherine Gilbert Murdock' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dairy Queen</a> made it to ALA's list of best YA books in 2007, so I decided to give it a try in spite of the awful cover and title. I was not disappointed.<br/><br/>15-year-old D.J. is forced to ta</span>
  <span id="freeText6169522116194088925" style="display:none">After being burned MANY times by crap YA books, I made a decision to only read those that at some point earned critical recognition (if I judged books by GR reviewer's ratings, I suspect I would have to work my way through nonsense like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6339664.Hush__Hush__Hush__Hush___1_" title="Hush, Hush (Hush, Hush, #1) by Becca Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener">Hush, Hush</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3975774.Evermore__The_Immortals___1_" title="Evermore (The Immortals, #1) by Alyson Noel" rel="nofollow noopener">Evermore</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1254951.The_Luxe__Luxe___1_" title="The Luxe (Luxe, #1) by Anna Godbersen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Luxe</a> and I am not sure I am up for it any more). <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16178.Dairy_Queen__Dairy_Queen___1_" title="Dairy Queen (Dairy Queen, #1) by Catherine Gilbert Murdock" rel="nofollow noopener">Dairy Queen</a> made it to ALA's list of best YA books in 2007, so I decided to give it a try in spite of the awful cover and title. I was not disappointed.<br /><br />15-year-old D.J. is forced to take over the lion's share of work on her family's small dairy farm after her father is injured. She is overwhelmed by milking, cleaning out the barn, mowing and haying, with almost no help but her younger brother's. In fact she is so overwhelmed, that she doesn't realize that her life at the moment has no direction or point. This is pointed to her by a lazy and arrogant Brian, the rival high school's quarterback, who is sent to D.J.'s farm to help her out, learn work ethics, and get some football training. Strangely enough, Brian has something to teach D.J. too - to look at her life style closer, to do some soul-searching, to become a better communicator.<br /><br />I can't say that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16178.Dairy_Queen__Dairy_Queen___1_" title="Dairy Queen (Dairy Queen, #1) by Catherine Gilbert Murdock" rel="nofollow noopener">Dairy Queen</a> is a mind-blowing kind of book. It's not really edgy or a dark "issue book." And that's a good thing. This is a novel about balancing family responsibilities and personal desires, about what it is to be a good person, and about importance of open communication in a family. D.J. is a very likable narrator, self-deprecating, hard-working, honest. She, along with the rest of the characters, feels very real and relatable. The teen romance is very well done too. It is realistic, doesn't overwhelm the story and never becomes cheesy or sappy, which is very important to me. I will undoubtedly read the next book in this 3-part series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6169522116194088925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=easy-read">easy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=lol">lol</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1926863334" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3464610831016790211">A very cute story about a 15 turning 16 year old girl named DJ who has only ever known life in her dad’s farm. She’s responsible, does what everyone expects of her, obedient and hardworking. Not much different from the cows she milks every day.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>“And that’s what put me to sleep. Thinking about cows or elephant poops.” </b>
</i>(LMAO!)<br/><br/>One day she decides she doesn’t want to be a cow anymore (and I mean this in a completely metaphorically way, so chill!)^^ and that’s where the plot becomes really interes</span>
  <span id="freeText3464610831016790211" style="display:none">A very cute story about a 15 turning 16 year old girl named DJ who has only ever known life in her dad’s farm. She’s responsible, does what everyone expects of her, obedient and hardworking. Not much different from the cows she milks every day.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“And that’s what put me to sleep. Thinking about cows or elephant poops.” </b>
</i>(LMAO!)<br /><br />One day she decides she doesn’t want to be a cow anymore (and I mean this in a completely metaphorically way, so chill!)^^ and that’s where the plot becomes really interesting. <br /><br />Written in a very candid and genuine manner in the POV of DJ herself as a journal for her English requirement to redeem her flunked grade, the story, I think, is very genuine and the voice of the narrative truly sounded as if it’s written by a young farm girl and this is probably what made the entire story simply adorable. It's also heartwarming and inspiring. As Uncle Walt Whitman once said: <b>
  <i> “Simplicity is the glory of expression.” </i>
</b></span>

<div id="review_172348988" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172348988" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172348988?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172348988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8225950643445323866"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>When I finally found a spare two minutes to sit down and start reading this book, I suddenly ended up drawn in for a couple of hours discovering that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16178.Dairy_Queen__Dairy_Queen___1_' title='Dairy Queen (Dairy Queen, #1) by Catherine Gilbert Murdock' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dairy Queen</a> is just as ridiculously funny, silly, and heartwarming as everyone had told me it was. And strangely inspirational too - I love anyone who dares to break the mold, especially young females who challenge gender stereotypes and go their own way. <br/><br/>I will admit that I am not the biggest fan of chick lit novels, so I should warn you that </span>
  <span id="freeText8225950643445323866" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>When I finally found a spare two minutes to sit down and start reading this book, I suddenly ended up drawn in for a couple of hours discovering that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16178.Dairy_Queen__Dairy_Queen___1_" title="Dairy Queen (Dairy Queen, #1) by Catherine Gilbert Murdock" rel="nofollow noopener">Dairy Queen</a> is just as ridiculously funny, silly, and heartwarming as everyone had told me it was. And strangely inspirational too - I love anyone who dares to break the mold, especially young females who challenge gender stereotypes and go their own way. <br><br>I will admit that I am not the biggest fan of chick lit novels, so I should warn you that this would probably never have got five stars from me, and the fact that it got four stars should not be taken lightly when I'm dishing it out in this genre. This book has all the elements you could want from a light-hearted, teen read: a funny, likeable and slightly snarky protagonist, cute boys, some family troubles - nothing too heavy, romance, friendships, insecurities and overcoming them... this stands out for me amongst others of its kind and I will give it the best compliment I can by saying that if you're a fan of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/65189.Louise_Rennison" title="Louise Rennison" rel="nofollow noopener">Louise Rennison</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/173491.E__Lockhart" title="E. Lockhart" rel="nofollow noopener">E. Lockhart</a> and/or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3095893.Stephanie_Perkins" title="Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephanie Perkins</a>, I can see no reason why you wouldn't love this.<br><br>D.J. Shwenk is a great character. You know why I think she is such a great character? Because she does sport and farming - two things that interest me about as much as Kim Kardashian's "novel" - and yet she still manages to keep my attention from the very first chapter. It takes A LOT to literally make someone laugh out loud while reading, as in, to actually pause and giggle stupidly to oneself and think if Big Brother was watching right now I would be arrested and locked away forever (am I paranoid? are these weird thoughts?). Anyway, this novel does this repeatedly and I'm glad I didn't read it in public.<br><br>I put this book off for two reasons, 1) I never thought I would enjoy a book about either sport or farming, never mind both! And 2) I've been busy reading the dark, disturbing, depressing, supernatural and fantasy books, which is all very well but sometimes we need a little bright happiness from our novels. This delivers, trust me, this delivers.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="8225950643445323866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1397992045" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1397992045" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1397992045?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=awesome-heroines">awesome-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=don-t-be-fooled-by-the-cover">don-t-be-fooled-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=physical-book-wishlist-want-it-need">physical-book-wishlist-want-it-need</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1397992045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18244402008868181163"><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>That's one advantage to not talking. After a while people stop talking back.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I swear, I <i>swear</i> to you....I am not a snob. Really!! Swear!! But come on...look at this cover. It's a cow. In a tiara. With a blue sky in the background and named after a restaurant I love. What's a girl to think when she sees this? Oh well, guess it's a moot point...<br/><br/><a href='http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/moopoint_zpse2boevpu.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443622176ra/16386601.gif' alt=' photo moopoint_zpse2boevpu.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Because this book was <b>fabulous</b>. (okay, I was guna use that GIF anyway because duh, friends, but it just worked out so well ;) )<br/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>Basically </b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText18244402008868181163" style="display:none"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>That's one advantage to not talking. After a while people stop talking back.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I swear, I <i>swear</i> to you....I am not a snob. Really!! Swear!! But come on...look at this cover. It's a cow. In a tiara. With a blue sky in the background and named after a restaurant I love. What's a girl to think when she sees this? Oh well, guess it's a moot point...<br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/moopoint_zpse2boevpu.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443622176ra/16386601.gif" alt=" photo moopoint_zpse2boevpu.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Because this book was <b>fabulous</b>. (okay, I was guna use that GIF anyway because duh, friends, but it just worked out so well ;) )<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>Basically what it came down to was that my life sucked. It sucked even more than it had before Brian showed up, because now I knew it.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>This book, while funny and outwardly mocking in and of itself, was also surprisingly <b>deep</b>, full of values that aren't always put first in a teenager's life. D.J.'s voice is one that, while a little different at first, is one that I think many young girls could relate to. Hell, <i>I</i> could relate to it. <br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/stock-footage-beautiful-girl-lying-on-the-meadow-and-dreaming-enjoy-nature-close-up-slow-motion-footage_zpsggnibzis.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443624875i/16386957.jpg" alt=" photo stock-footage-beautiful-girl-lying-on-the-meadow-and-dreaming-enjoy-nature-close-up-slow-motion-footage_zpsggnibzis.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Think about it-No, I'm not a farmer, and no, I wasn't <i>totally</i> socially awkward ever, but I had trouble finding my voice. And not everyone runs into this problem, I know that. But, hey, I grew up in the country, and I went to a school where driving your tractor there wouldn't raise eyebrows. It was Hick City people. The kids were very kind, very well brought up for a public school, so it should come as no shock to you that when my parents ripped me out of that happy (and horrible academically wise) school away from all my friends <i>just</i> as I was getting my braces and figuring out who I was (thanks mom and dad, <i>really</i>), <b>I had trouble finding my place at the elite schools in town</b>. I bet you're asking why they pulled me out. I'll tell you why in a few words: Soccer program (as in, ours was nonexistent and I was REALLY GOOD) and academics. I couldn't go into high school without a better level of academics and not knowing the in town program and it's people and coaches. ANYWAY.<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>I hate it when people make fun of me and it turns out they're right.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>So, when I started in town at a tiny private school with a totally different grading scale and girls that were <i>far</i> more advanced than I in 7th grade, I found that <b>I was standing on the outside of the circle with very little to say</b> besides a literal smile and nod of the head for everything they deemed important. Ah, youth. I want to incinerate some of those moments. But that's my whole point-I knew what I wanted to say, and I rarely agreed with what they were going on and on about. I had my own opinions, but <b>I was both too shy and too backwards</b> (at the time) to express them...so I just looked wild-eyed at them and nodded my head so as to fit in. Yeah. That worked out <i>great</i>. But, again, the point-I am just like D.J. in this instance...and I think many young girls are, as well.<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>How could a guy who was such a jerk, how could he act so nice?</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_mpzlorgoIH1rx35huo1_500_zps1xg2kov0.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443624918ra/16386964.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mpzlorgoIH1rx35huo1_500_zps1xg2kov0.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>And that's why I loved this cute little story so much. Yeah, the writing was great and the boy was great (Brian!!!!) and it was so so funny...but I fell for D.J.. She's this girl who thinks so little of herself, yet she's so very strong and smart and determined. She has trouble expressing herself, even though she has so much to say. And I loved that. <b>I loved her voice</b> and her thoughtful sentences and the way she spoke to you as if you were a friend. It was a journey of discovering herself and finding out that not everybody is what you'd imagine them to be. And...most importantly, <b>this chick tries out for football</b>. And then she falls for the rival team's quarterback. Be still my star-crossed heart.<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>I couldn't help wondering if maybe it had something to do with me, like our water fight and all. But then I realized that I was totally stupid and there's no way it could <i>ever</i> be about me, not in a million years, not if I was the only girl on the entire planet.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>Now, I know what you're thinking: What a weird concept. I know, I thought so too. But when she decides to try out for football, it actually became my favorite part...because, you know, she has to play that rival football team MUAHA! lol. I'm weird today. Anyway! She decides to train Brian all summer after some prompting from a family friend because she trained with her brothers who are now big names in college football. What starts out as reluctant training and working together on the farm becomes a highlight of each of their weeks, and something so much more. <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/giphy%2040_zpsu9rwrtzl.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443623872ra/16386857.gif" alt=" photo giphy 40_zpsu9rwrtzl.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The whole book D.J. is trying to prove her worth to herself, that she's not just some cow that does what everybody says, and when she finally finds a purpose, playing football for her school's team, it helps her to feel vindicated and strong and <b>worthy of people's admiration</b>. I think that's where <i>my</i> admiration came in for her...what a brave (and hilarious) thing to do.<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>I saw something I wanted to do and I decided to do it. The feeling of freedom this gave me-I can't even describe it. It was my decision. I chose it. I am not a cow.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>So, you know, despite my earlier trepidation of how this story would be, I got just as many feels from this as any other book: Angst, fear, butterflies, sadness, giddiness, family issues, this book had it all. Near the end my stomach was in such a big bundle of nerves I almost couldn't sleep. And I guess that's my other life lesson...<b>you can't judge a book by it's cover</b>. Sometimes you find the best stories with the worst covers...it just happens. But I'm sure I'll continue to make that mistake...but I'll do my best to shake the habit.<br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><br><a title="Facebook" href="https://www.facebook.com/starcrossedbookblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055977i/15660595.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="Twitter" href="https://twitter.com/starcrossedblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660580.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="RSS" href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/starcrossedbookblog/METU" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660581.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="BLOGLOVIN" href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/star-crossed-book-blog-13035961" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660579.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>************************<br><br><br><br><br><br>Surprisingly deep with <b>wonderful values</b>...I can't wait to read more of this series.<br><br>And, you know...<br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/Cows-sm_zpsujqyacff.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443530993i/16373561.jpg" alt=" photo Cows-sm_zpsujqyacff.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Just sayin'<br><br>RTC</span>

<div id="review_112089704" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112089704" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1233686-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334791106p2/1233686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112089704?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/1233686-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=not-mine-library">not-mine-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=ya-summer-challange-2011">ya-summer-challange-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112089704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2736547934917665316"><i>Dairy Queen</i> has got to be the best book hidden behind the worst cover/title ever. This isn’t a book I would have given a second glance at if it weren’t for so many Goodreads friends raving over it. Even looking past the cover, the synopsis here doesn’t sound great. One special summer in which our young protagonist, D.J. Schwenk spends time with a guy who is “out of her league”, figures out some family issues and goes out for the boys football team? This has the potential to be quirky in an oh-so</span>
  <span id="freeText2736547934917665316" style="display:none"><i>Dairy Queen</i> has got to be the best book hidden behind the worst cover/title ever. This isn’t a book I would have given a second glance at if it weren’t for so many Goodreads friends raving over it. Even looking past the cover, the synopsis here doesn’t sound great. One special summer in which our young protagonist, D.J. Schwenk spends time with a guy who is “out of her league”, figures out some family issues and goes out for the boys football team? This has the potential to be quirky in an oh-so-annoying way. But it isn’t. Not at all. And I am kicking myself for not reading this book sooner than now.<br /><br />To start with, D.J. is refreshing and a pleasure to read about. Author Catherine Gilbert Murdock writes D.J. in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/301082.Dead_Until_Dark" rel="nofollow noopener">Sookie Stackhouse</a> style. That is, she just happily rambles about her day, her thoughts and feelings on just about everything in such a friendly, conversational manner that before you know it you are completely hooked. Unlike Sookie though, D.J. is figuring out her purpose and goals in life. Also, this series will not be more than a trilogy, so we know her blathering will have a point and eventually lead us to (hopefully!) a satisfying conclusion. D.J. is every bit the tomboy who lives and works on a dairy farm, is athletic, and much like any boy, is very uncomfortable experiencing and expressing emotions. We get to meet her family who are just as tough, strong, sensitive and emotionally unenlightened as D.J. is. Of course YA covers are misleading, but I still think it’s odd for this book to have such a weird, whimsical cover when there really isn’t anything weird or whimsical about D.J. <br /><br /><i>Dairy Queen</i> is simply one of those books which gets so many things right, it’s hard to articulate what makes it so special. I love that D.J. follows her desires not in an effort to prove a point, or impress someone or rebel. She merely attempts to figure out what she wants in life and endeavors to follow her dreams. There is a great message in this novel of being true to yourself. <br /><br />And did I mention this book is also about football? Lots and lots of football (oh yeah!) Murdock does a fantastic job of describing the sport, but it’s clear that she really isn’t a fan when she mentions D.J.’s old brother/football hero Bill attending Minnesota. Yeah, it’s cool he’s playing for a NCAA team and all, but really <i>Minnesota</i>?? Just about the worst team in the Big Ten. I could understand if the book was based in Minnesota, or Murdock had special ties to that school (who knows, maybe she does?) But <i>Dairy Queen</i> takes place in Wisconsin, which has a perfectly respectable state university and football team of their own. A team that is so good, I always have a tight knot of anxiety in my stomach when my beloved Buckeyes play them. Ah, well. <br /><br />Besides being proud of her brother for attending Minnesota (because for fucks sake, they are terrible!) <i>Dairy Queen</i> is a flawless and enjoyable book. It is definitely one I recommend, even for people who are not football fans. Really, the sports stuff isn’t so overwhelming for those of you who just aren’t into it. For the rest of us, it’s got just enough to make you count down the days till kickoff. That is, if you aren’t already =)<br /><br />UPDATE: This series rocks! Just finished the final installment, <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6318426.Front_and_Center__Dairy_Queen___3_" title="Front and Center (Dairy Queen, #3) by Catherine Gilbert Murdock" rel="nofollow noopener">Front and Center</a> and loved it. Going back to rate each book in this trilogy 5 stars (8/22/11)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2736547934917665316" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_198245023" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198245023" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198245023?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Vinaya by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=books-i-loved">books-i-loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=hmm-that-was-interesting">hmm-that-was-interesting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=speshul-snowflake">speshul-snowflake</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=ya-fiction">ya-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=surprised-me">surprised-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198245023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15432975569623326256">Back in the good old days when Net Galley was a bountiful god instead of the clutch-fisted miser it is becoming, I used to go wild requesting every galley I could find. One of the books I requested was a novel about a girl who plays baseball on a boy's team. I never did read more than fifty pages of that one - it was pretty dry, but it did make me a little apprehensive about reading sports-related stories. Which is weird because I LOVE sports-related movies. I couldn't tell you the rules of Amer</span>
  <span id="freeText15432975569623326256" style="display:none">Back in the good old days when Net Galley was a bountiful god instead of the clutch-fisted miser it is becoming, I used to go wild requesting every galley I could find. One of the books I requested was a novel about a girl who plays baseball on a boy's team. I never did read more than fifty pages of that one - it was pretty dry, but it did make me a little apprehensive about reading sports-related stories. Which is weird because I LOVE sports-related movies. I couldn't tell you the rules of American football if you held a gun to my head, but something about the intensity and excitement with which a bunch of men toss a ball around just gets me all happy. So it's pretty amazing that Catherine Gilbert Murdock managed to induce the same excitement in me without visual aids and eye candy.<br /><br />There are just so many reasons to love Dairy Queen. I could go on and on all night and still not capture the magic of D.J. Schwenk. But I'm sure as hell gonna try. <br /><br />The Schwenks are not what you'd call a talkative family. They're hardworking and "athletically gifted", but verbosity is not one of their talents. There's a lot of currents flowing under the still water, but it's not until Brian Nelson swaggers into DJ's life that she really begins to think about where her life is going. <br /><br />That summary might give you the impression that luuurve changes our heroine like a butterfly from a chrysalis, or whatever, but that's not how it goes. What really, really <b>works</b> for Dairy Queen is how unbelievably <i>real</i> it is. DJ has a very distinctive voice. She's a hick, through and through, and it comes through very clearly in her words and her attitudes. But she's smart and more interestingly, she's introspective. I love introspective heroines... I don't mean the ones who angst endlessly without ever growing up, but the ones who use the incidents in their life to grow and develop as a person. Nobody does this better than DJ Schwenk. She handles her hard life (and it is HARD, believe me!) with grace and panache. <br /><br />Every character in this book could be someone you meet on the street. Who says Everyman can't be interesting. Murdock takes the concept of perfectly ordinary people leading perfectly ordinary lives and makes you beg for more. And if that's not talent, I don't know what is. The characters in this story are flawed, amazing and interesting, simply for being so relatable. <br /><br />There's Brian - he <i>could</i> have turned out to be a cardboard-cutout handsome jock, but there's more to him than that. There's the nasty, snobby, spoiled side, with the whining and the unwillingness to take responsibility. And there's the admirable, friendly side, with the willingness to apologize and the slowly developing friendship with a girl from a rival school who's not the most attractive, amazing girl on earth. <br /><br />The same applies to DJ's father, the cause of so much turmoil in her life, her almost mute brother, her ultra-busy mother, the brothers who abandoned her, her mixed-up best friend. With a few anecdotes here and there, Murdock manages to make these people come alive in all their flawlessly flawed glory. <br /><br />And at the heart of it all is DJ Schwenk. Big and bold and beautiful, even when she barely realizes it, so very ordinary, and yet extraordinary in her sweetness and her thoughtfulness and her ability and desire to change and think outside the box. DJ is a heroine that I might henceforth measure all heroines by - take that, you nasty size zero princesses! <br /><br />As DJ says herself, although the book might be about football, football is just a metaphor for all the things that change over the course of one summer. And yet, I can't deny that I thoroughly, in a very pop-movie way, enjoyed the thrashing Red Bend gives Hawley under DJ's direction. The scenes are tightly paced and excitingly written and I felt like I was SO ready to go out there and wear a foam finger and cheer my heart out for this little high school football team. <br /><br />I've already made my way through the second book in the series, and I gotta tell you, it only gets better. This is coming-of-age like no coming-of-age before, romance like no romance before, family drama like no family drama before. If you haven't read this book, I would wholeheartedly recommend that you go get it right this minute, because every second you waste thinking about it is a precious second you could be spending getting to know the one, the only, DJ Schwenk!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15432975569623326256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_185039572" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/185039572" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/185039572?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Maja (The Nocturnal Library) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa">Limonessa</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2011">reviewed-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=all-the-right-choices">all-the-right-choices</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer185039572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11555669733209377336">I never thought I’d have fun reading about a belching contest of all things, but that’s exactly what happened. Murdock’s Dairy Queen is just the kind of YA I can truly enjoy: loads of fun on the surface, yet if you remember to look a little deeper, for the most part it’s not funny at all. <br/><br/>I noticed a long time ago that authors often have problems with creating characters that are quite average. On one side, most of them don’t even want to because they’re convinced that nobody likes to read about</span>
  <span id="freeText11555669733209377336" style="display:none">I never thought I’d have fun reading about a belching contest of all things, but that’s exactly what happened. Murdock’s Dairy Queen is just the kind of YA I can truly enjoy: loads of fun on the surface, yet if you remember to look a little deeper, for the most part it’s not funny at all. <br /><br />I noticed a long time ago that authors often have problems with creating characters that are quite average. On one side, most of them don’t even want to because they’re convinced that nobody likes to read about average people. On the other, even when they try, they usually don’t know how. Sometimes you can just see that’s what the author intended to do, especially in YA, but the characters end up being either too smart or too stupid to live, thus remaining completely unrealistic and two-dimensional. That is not the case with Catherine Murdock. In my opinion, she was successful. D.J. always does the right thing for herself, but that doesn’t mean that she’s too smart. She’s not very pretty or very social, either. But Murdock knows how to make you care for her and see her in a completely different light. The thing I liked most about D.J. is that she never once made me feel frustrated or angry because I always knew that she was doing her best, even when it wasn’t enough. <br /><br />Stylistically speaking, at first glance, the writing was a little strange. I was bothered by it at first, but then I started discovering things about D.J. and I realized that it needed to be adapted to the narrator. D.J. flunked her English class because she was too busy working on the family farm. All those awkward sentences (kind of like mine, but worse) and words that kept repeating again and again made things sound more authentic. In other words, once I realized that Murdock did it on purpose, and it DID take me a while, I liked it. <br /><br />Phew. Let me tell you, flirting is never easy, but having any sort of romantic conversation while shoveling cow poop is next to impossible. And yet D.J. and Brian managed to do it, and it was awkward, adorable and everything else it was supposed to be. I loved the two of them together and I loved that the focus wasn't on the romance at all. <br /><br />I can’t wait to read the next two books! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11555669733209377336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

But ultimately, the insanely true voice (by turns very funny and very touching) and nice working of common themes through the book (saying this is a realistic YA novel about cows and football is at once the truest and least true thing you could every say) makes me give this five stars.<br/><br/>Definitely just -- great voice. <br/><br/><br/>***wondering why </span>
  <span id="freeText3486869931271654315" style="display:none">I debated for a long time whether I wanted to put this one in my five star section, because I didn't think the ending was as strong as I thought it could have been. But ultimately, the insanely true voice (by turns very funny and very touching) and nice working of common themes through the book (saying this is a realistic YA novel about cows and football is at once the truest and least true thing you could every say) makes me give this five stars.<br /><br />Definitely just -- great voice. <br /><br /><br />***wondering why all my reviews are five stars? <div id="review_139214070" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139214070" />
    <a title="Flannery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/652877-flannery"><img alt="Flannery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312843258p2/652877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139214070?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=kcls">kcls</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139214070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18329569827943357350">DJ Schwenk is a teenage girl growing up on a dairy farm in rural Wisconsin. Her family suffers from a lack of communication and the departure of her two older brothers, along with her father's hip surgery, have put even more strain on DJ. Her workload at school is overwhelming when she adds in all the work she has to do to keep the family farm running. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16178.Dairy_Queen__Dairy_Queen___1_' title='Dairy Queen (Dairy Queen, #1) by Catherine Gilbert Murdock' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dairy Queen</a> chronicles a few weeks of her summer vacation...if you can call it a vacation. <br/><br/>If you have to listen to professors talk about stuff l</span>
  <span id="freeText18329569827943357350" style="display:none">DJ Schwenk is a teenage girl growing up on a dairy farm in rural Wisconsin. Her family suffers from a lack of communication and the departure of her two older brothers, along with her father's hip surgery, have put even more strain on DJ. Her workload at school is overwhelming when she adds in all the work she has to do to keep the family farm running. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16178.Dairy_Queen__Dairy_Queen___1_" title="Dairy Queen (Dairy Queen, #1) by Catherine Gilbert Murdock" rel="nofollow noopener">Dairy Queen</a> chronicles a few weeks of her summer vacation...if you can call it a vacation. <br /><br />If you have to listen to professors talk about stuff like substantive due process and prescriptive easements for 3-4 hours a night, this is the type of audiobook to listen to on the way there and back. Honestly, my heart was so warmed up by the time I got there every night that I could handle it with no complaints. And the narrator had a pretty good (not perfect)Wisconsin accent. It made me miss my friends from the midwest a ton. (Especially you, Maureen-who-only-occasionally-signs-on-goodreads-and-who-I-promise-to-call-back-soon!) It also made me miss my NCCC days, where we worked hard, worked out a lot, and sweat a ton. I miss going out to do something where I could see visible results and feel good after the fact. I miss working outside and I was (dare I say it) jealous of the farm work DJ had to do.<br /><br />Anyway, this book is adorable. DJ is adorable. And I definitely recommend this book to anyone who likes a realistic YA book. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_172201009" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172201009" />
    <a title="Limonessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa"><img alt="Limonessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424025988p2/4147373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172201009?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Limonessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Limonessa" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa">Limonessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172201009" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1206424269433473612">....why couldn't Murdock just continue to write YA instead of delving into middle grade? Sorry, Ms. Murdock, I am not saying <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10043376.Wisdom_s_Kiss' title='Wisdom's Kiss by Catherine Gilbert Murdock' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wisdom's Kiss</a> was bad but this is SO much better. Actually it was pretty great, as soon as I finished it I went online to order the other two books in the series.<br/><br/>All because of DJ. <br/>DJ Schwenk is no Barbie doll. She is tall, big, strong and runs her family's farm. Despite being in high school, she is overwhelmed by the daily chores required for the normal upkeep of a farm, </span>
  <span id="freeText1206424269433473612" style="display:none">....why couldn't Murdock just continue to write YA instead of delving into middle grade? Sorry, Ms. Murdock, I am not saying <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10043376.Wisdom_s_Kiss" title="Wisdom's Kiss by Catherine Gilbert Murdock" rel="nofollow noopener">Wisdom's Kiss</a> was bad but this is SO much better. Actually it was pretty great, as soon as I finished it I went online to order the other two books in the series.<br /><br />All because of DJ. <br />DJ Schwenk is no Barbie doll. She is tall, big, strong and runs her family's farm. Despite being in high school, she is overwhelmed by the daily chores required for the normal upkeep of a farm, a burden she acquired after her father injured himself and is therefore unable to do hard work. Aside from being farmers, the Schwenks are also good at playing football and DJ is no exception. So when Brian Nelson, the quarterback of a rival school is coerced by his coach to show up at her doorstep looking for training and to help with the farm, DJ cannot but accept, hoping to teach the guy a lesson. But, as it turns out, it will be DJ to learn more than she bargained for out of this lesson, about herself, her family and the importance of communication.<br /><br />So after a brief surfing interlude with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6989576.Raw_Blue" title="Raw Blue by Kirsty Eagar" rel="nofollow noopener">Raw Blue</a>, here goes another typical Italian national sport, football. <br />NOT. Football is, in Italy, just about as widespread as Mountain Dew and Starbucks (yes, you can start pitying now, we have none of those here). Consequently, my knowledge of either slang or rules related to this game is... close to zero, I'd say (I only know names of players that the Kardashians have dated so... pretty many actually). <br />BUT, in Dairy Queen, it didn't matter. To be honest, I have to confess that my interest got piqued and I am developing a certain attraction towards the game. But again, I think it might be all because of DJ. This book is so good primarily for its main character. <br />Written in first person, DJ is a truly amazing voice in the ranks of YA heroines. She is neither beautiful nor particularly brilliant but she is so honest, authentic and just.... genuine that it was impossible for me not to sympathize with her and with her predicaments. And cheer for her all the way. I mean, this girl plays football, how cool is that?<br /><br />And while I would define this as a great, fresh and fast summer read (I read it at the beach and I have to say the cow cover perfectly matched with the surroundings), it is far, far from shallow. DJ's dysfunctional family and friends guide us through the rules of personal communication, familiar love and friendship beyond social strata, giving it a depth hidden behind the simple, yet clever tone and writing style.<br /> <br />I really enjoyed it, it pleasantly surprised me and I'm looking forward to knowing what happens to DJ next! Definitely recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1206424269433473612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_199461225" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/199461225" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/199461225?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer199461225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5397438678408467843"><i>
  <b>“If this was a movie or something I’d give this awesome speech and everyone would cheer and it would be great. But it wasn’t a movie-it was my life. And I don’t have much to say in the best of situations.”</b>
</i><br/><br/><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br/>If you need me, I’m gonna be in Schwenksville. Also… this review is brought to you by the letter ‘R’… for <i>REAL</i><br/> <br/><b>High Points.</b><br/>This book is <i>re-</i>… OK, I’ll stop that right there. DJ Swchenk. Brian. Summer lovin’. A girl with ambitions. Diversity. Cows. Pick-up trucks. </span>
  <span id="freeText5397438678408467843" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“If this was a movie or something I’d give this awesome speech and everyone would cheer and it would be great. But it wasn’t a movie-it was my life. And I don’t have much to say in the best of situations.”</b>
</i><br /><br /><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br />If you need me, I’m gonna be in Schwenksville. Also… this review is brought to you by the letter ‘R’… for <i>REAL</i><br /> <br /><b>High Points.</b><br />This book is <i>re-</i>… OK, I’ll stop that right there. DJ Swchenk. Brian. Summer lovin’. A girl with ambitions. Diversity. Cows. Pick-up trucks. Water fights. Painting. Brothers. Nervous phone calls. Head butts. Brownies. <br /><br /><b>Low Point.</b><br />(Prepare for a ramble, this actually is only one low point. But I just like the <s>sound</s> look of my own <s>voice</s> words.)<br />This year I got tricked into staying up and watching the Superbowl. I was told “<i>It’s like rugby. Except you can’t really see their face because they wear protection so you can’t objectify the players like you do with rugby. But apart from that… there’s no difference</i>.”<br />Disclaimer: There are more reasons to why I watch and enjoy rugby than the prospect of Jonny Wilkinson in tiny shorts. <s>Like Toby Flood, Delon Armitage, Mark Cueto, Chris Ashton and when we play Scotland… everyone but especially Richie Gray but don’t tell anyone because I can’t love the enemy….in tiny shorts</s>. Like I get to watch it with my dad and my brother and it makes me all goosepimply when the crowd starts singing ‘Swing Low Sweet Chariot’ at Twickenham. <br />But anyway… it turns out there is a <i>huge</i> difference between American Football and rugby. I get far too into games of rugby (I could have given Martin Johnson a run for his money in the scowling stakes this past Six Nations *grumbles*). I know rugby. I understand rugby (well, I’m not an expert and I still have to ask my granddad, who gives me an exasperated look and states “This is why girls shouldn’t watch sport” or “The effin’ ref, Jo, that’s what’s happening.”) sometimes but I understand about 95% of what is happening… which is good <s>for a girl</s>). <br />I do not know American football and I do not understand American football. I tried to watch <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0758745/" rel="nofollow noopener">Friday Night Lights</a> but every time Kyle Chandler was on the screen all I could think about was <a href="http://epguides.com/EarlyEdition/cast.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">Early Edition</a> and <i>that</i> episode of Grey’s Anatomy and <i>that</i> can of worms was opened and… yeah.<br />So this book often lost me in that sense…. But it didn’t take away any of the enjoyment, but I just think it would have increased the enjoyment if I actually knew what the eff was going on. <br /><br /><b>Heroine.</b><br />OK, I’m pretty sure I <s>am</s> <i>was</i> DJ Schwenk in another life. She is awkward, she isn’t all that clever but she is so <s>real</s> genuine as a teenager and she was so believable. Also she is gutsy and cynical and not a girly girl without being too overwhelming or ‘YEAH. LOOK AT ME. I’M A MASSIVE TOMBOY AND FEMINIST. WHATCHA GONNA DO, HUH? YEAH. I’M GONNA PUNCH YOU IF YOU LOOK AT MY BOOBS’ because, to me, that’s just as bad as a YA heroine being simpering and blarrgh.<br />The line isn’t that fine between these two categories and I wish more authors would take a leaf out of Ms Gilbert Murdock’s book and create characters that experience feelings that every day people have but not lose themselves completely when things go belly-up.<br />DJ is such a refreshing heroine and I can’t wait to find out more about her. <br /><br /><b>Best Friend.</b><br />I really hope we see more of Amber in the next book… such an original relationship and I can’t wait to see where it will go.<br /><br /><b>Love Interest.</b><br />Brian, you are as cute as a button. And even though you’re flirtytirty relationship with DJ was very subtle it was still present and so cute… and surprisingly swoonworthy.<br />From other reviews of this book I have read, I thought this book was going to be a love-free zone, so I was pleasantly surprised when I ended up getting a bit tummy-flippy at certain parts.<br />Again, I don’t think your story is finished yet and I bet you continue to make me go weak at the knees and wish I knew more about American football so I could understand a single word you said and not just focus on you painting barns topless.<br />Which I didn’t do. Nuh-uh not me.<br /><br /><b>Theme Tune.</b><br /><br /><s>
  <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6AwXKJoKJz4&amp;ob=av2e" rel="nofollow noopener">Milkshake- Kelis</a>
</s><br />HAHA…I’m kidding. <br />*looks shifty*<br />I thought it would be really difficult to find a song about this book because surely there are hardly any songs about cows and dairy and farming… right? WRONG.<br />I found lots.<br />But I’m saving them for t’other books in this series which I can’t wait to get my grubby mitts on. Although… they might not even be about farming. But whatever. <br /><br />So here’s Numero 1.<br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rAn_2SdADoc" rel="nofollow noopener">For All The Cows- Foo Fighters. </a><br /><br />Because I love the Foo Fighters and I have seen them about a million times live and whenever I have seen them they were with my best friends at the time and Dave Grohl will always have a special place in my <s>pants</s> heart.<br /><br /><b>Boy/<s>Girl</s> Angst Level.</b><br />2/10. YOU GUYS, I have found a book with absolutely <i>no</i> boy angst. Well, OK. About two pages. But it’s completely OK, because D.J is a <i>normal</i> girl who is <i>real</i> and thus doesn’t have approximately a million chapters of ‘WHY DOESN’T HE LOVE ME?’ She has normal hang-ups but doesn’t blabber on about them. She gets on with things which is what normal and real life people do and it’s awkward and sometimes I had to read this book through my fingers <s>because it reminded me so much of myself</s> but it’s <u>real</u>. And I loved it. <br /><br /><br /><b>Sadness Scale.</b><br />5/10. This was a tough one because there were some parts that really made me quite sad and it was kind of like when you’re in the cinema and you get a bit choked up at a part and you look to the person next to you and it’s not affected them at all. And then you feel a bit silly for getting a bit worked up. That was like looking at D.J’s life. It wasn’t that she didn’t let things bother her.. but she just didn’t let other people know they were bothering her.<br />Oh, I just loved D.J. <br /><br /><br /><b>Recommended For.</b><br />People who are looking for a realistic fiction where a girl is just a girl and a boy is just a boy. No one changes into something at night, no one has a taste for blood and no one has the fate of the world resting on their skinny shoulders. People who were awkward. People who have ever <i>dreamed</i> of <s>being taunted with a jock strap by a sweaty boy</s> of doing something that you love. People who have older brothers. People who have always wanted to live on a farm. People who like American Football… I’m presuming the depiction is quite correct? People who love brownies that you can eat like soup. People who collect animal skulls. People who wouldn’t know where to even begin if someone handed them a power hose. People who have ever used the excuse ‘Um, we were just doing sit ups Dad”. <br /></span>

<div id="review_102555785" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102555785" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102555785?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=sporty">sporty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102555785" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4431439357422180833">Dairy Queen by Catherine Gilbert Murdock is an absolutely awesome book. It was laugh out loud funny and truly engaging, but the thing that moves this book into the five-star category for me, is the fact that it was down-right inspiring. D.J. Schwenk has become one of my favorite female fictional characters. When I picked up this book, I didn’t think I’d enjoy it too much as I have no clue what it takes to work a farm and no idea how the game of football works… this book made me a fan of both. <br/><br/>I </span>
  <span id="freeText4431439357422180833" style="display:none">Dairy Queen by Catherine Gilbert Murdock is an absolutely awesome book. It was laugh out loud funny and truly engaging, but the thing that moves this book into the five-star category for me, is the fact that it was down-right inspiring. D.J. Schwenk has become one of my favorite female fictional characters. When I picked up this book, I didn’t think I’d enjoy it too much as I have no clue what it takes to work a farm and no idea how the game of football works… this book made me a fan of both. <br /><br />I loved D.J.’s dialog and how she constantly describes events, feelings and reactions in absolute extremes. For the most part, I find that technique irritating and distracting, but for some reason D.J. was able to pull it off when she’d say stuff like, <i>“it was the most embarrassing thing that happened to me in my whole life; it was the biggest lie in the whole world; it was the longest day I ever lived; it was the worst meal ever made; it was the most horrible thing that happened in my life,”</i> I would find myself smiling because it came across as endearing that fit perfectly with D.J.’s modest character.<br /><br />About the book…. D.J. Schwenk is a small town Wisconsin girl forced to work the family farm when her father suffers an injury, her brothers move on to college, and her mother is stuck working two jobs to make ends meet. She does her job and works long hours without voicing one word of compliant. And, as the story progresses you learn that it becomes a problem because she never communicates how she feels and what she wants out of life, she just lets her circumstance decide her fate. All that changes when Brian Nelson, the QB from D.J.’s rival high school, comes to work on the farm and ends up taking football lessons from her. As she trains Brian, she learns that there’s more she wants out of life and when something that really matters comes up, she needs to speak up.<br /><br />There were several scenes I found hilarious and inspiring and I never thought I’d say that I found a football game exciting, but there I was cheering on the characters in a preseason game. Who knew??!! There were so many things about this book that made it absolutely awesome, and I can’t wait for my turn in the library queue for the next book in the series to come in. Great story that will have you engaged and ultimately motivated. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4431439357422180833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer10639935718198744350">I’ve been home sick for two days the other week and during that time I read all three books of this series back to back and whenever I’m doing something like this I find it hard to come up a with a review for each single book since everything kind of blurs together and I’m having trouble distinguishing the different books in my head, so I’m just going to do one review for all three books and keep it general.<br/><br/>D.J. is one of those protagonists you just gotta love! She’s so likeable and easy to rela</span>
  <span id="freeText10639935718198744350" style="display:none">I’ve been home sick for two days the other week and during that time I read all three books of this series back to back and whenever I’m doing something like this I find it hard to come up a with a review for each single book since everything kind of blurs together and I’m having trouble distinguishing the different books in my head, so I’m just going to do one review for all three books and keep it general.<br /><br />D.J. is one of those protagonists you just gotta love! She’s so likeable and easy to relate to. I didn’t know what to expect when I first picked up the Dairy Queen and I certainly wouldn’t have expected to find such a heartwarming, gripping and funny story. I loved all three books, and every one of them had me perched at the edge of my seat, ready to jump up and yell "GO D.J. GO" because I had been so caught up in her story. All the characters of this series felt extremely real to me and I loved each one of them along with all their flaws. At some points the story made me laugh out loud, at some points I had to slap my forehead or even shut my book for a few minutes because I suffered from vicarious embarrassment and I just couldn’t take it anymore, at some points I was so angry on D.J.’s behalf that I wanted to kick something and at some points the story brought tears to my eyes. There’s also a cute romance included but only the story of the third book revolves to a larger extent around D.J.’s love live. <br /><br />This series is fun and sweet and I recommend it to everybody. A good piece of contemporary YA.<br /></span>
